This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\n    25→    /// that is associated with the task.\n    26→    /// The value of this field gets passed to all functions that are part of\n    27→    /// the vtable as the first parameter.\n    28→    data: *const (),\n    29→    /// Virtual function pointer table that customizes the behavior of this waker.\n    30→    vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable,\n    31→}\n    32→\n    33→impl RawWaker {\n    34→    /// Creates a new `RawWaker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\n    35→    ///\n    36→    /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\n    37→    /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\n    38→    /// that is associated with the task.\n    39→    /// The value of this pointer will get passed to all functions that are part\n    40→    /// of the `vtable` as the first parameter.\n    41→    ///\n    42→    /// It is important to consider that the `data` pointer must point to a\n    43→    /// thread safe type such as an `Arc<T: Send + Sync>`\n    44→    /// when used to construct a [`Waker`]. This restriction is lifted when\n    45→    /// constructing a [`LocalWaker`], which allows using types that do not implement\n    46→    /// <code>[Send] + [Sync]</code> like `Rc<T>`.\n    47→    ///\n    48→    /// The `vtable` customizes the behavior of a `Waker` which gets created\n    49→    /// from a `RawWaker`. For each operation on the `Waker`, the associated\n    50→    /// function in the `vtable` of the underlying `RawWaker` will be called.\n    51→    #[inline]\n    52→    #[rustc_promotable]\n    53→    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    54→    #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    55→    #[must_use]\n    56→    pub const fn new(data: *const (), vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable) -> RawWaker {\n    57→        RawWaker { data, vtable }\n    58→    }\n    59→\n    60→    #[stable(feature = \"noop_waker\", since = \"1.85.0\")]\n    61→    const NOOP: RawWaker = {\n    62→        const VTABLE: RawWakerVTable = RawWakerVTable::new(\n    63→            // Cloning just returns a new no-op raw waker\n    64→            |_| RawWaker::NOOP,\n    65→            // `wake` does nothing\n    66→            |_| {},\n    67→            // `wake_by_ref` does nothing\n    68→            |_| {},\n    69→            // Dropping does nothing as we don't allocate anything\n    70→            |_| {},\n    71→        );\n    72→        RawWaker::new(ptr::null(), &VTABLE)\n    73→    };\n    74→}\n    75→\n    76→/// A virtual function pointer table (vtable) that specifies the behavior\n    77→/// of a [`RawWaker`].\n    78→///\n    79→/// The pointer passed to all functions inside the vtable is the `data` pointer\n    80→/// from the enclosing [`RawWaker`] object.\n    81→///\n    82→/// The functions inside this struct are only intended to be called on the `data`\n    83→/// pointer of a properly constructed [`RawWaker`] object from inside the\n    84→/// [`RawWaker`] implementation. Calling one of the contained functions using\n    85→/// any other `data` pointer will cause undefined behavior.\n    86→///\n    87→/// Note that while this type implements `PartialEq`, comparing function pointers, and hence\n    88→/// comparing structs like this that contain function pointers, is unreliable: pointers to the same\n    89→/// function can compare inequal (because functions are duplicated in multiple codegen units), and\n    90→/// pointers to *different* functions can compare equal (since identical functions can be\n    91→/// deduplicated within a codegen unit).\n    92→///\n    93→/// # Thread safety\n    94→/// If the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`Waker`] then\n    95→/// these functions must all be thread-safe (even though [`RawWaker`] is\n    96→/// <code>\\![Send] + \\![Sync]</code>). This is because [`Waker`] is <code>[Send] + [Sync]</code>,\n    97→/// and it may be moved to arbitrary threads or invoked by `&` reference. For example,\n    98→/// this means that if the `clone` and `drop` functions manage a reference count,\n    99→/// they must do so atomically.\n   100→///\n   101→/// However, if the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`LocalWaker`] instead, then\n   102→/// these functions don't need to be thread safe. /// Sets the value for the extension data on `Context`.\n   363→    #[inline]\n   364→    #[unstable(feature = \"context_ext\", issue = \"123392\")]\n   365→    pub const fn ext(self, data: &'a mut dyn Any) -> Self {\n   366→        Self { ext: ExtData::Some(data), ..self }\n   367→    }\n   368→\n   369→    /// Builds the `Context`.\n   370→    #[inline]\n   371→    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   372→    pub const fn build(self) -> Context<'a> {\n   373→        let ContextBuilder { waker, local_waker, ext, _marker, _marker2 } = self;\n   374→        Context { waker, local_waker, ext: AssertUnwindSafe(ext), _marker, _marker2 }\n   375→    }\n   376→}\n   377→\n   378→/// A `Waker` is a handle for waking up a task by notifying its executor that it\n   379→/// is ready to be run.\n   380→///\n   381→/// This handle encapsulates a [`RawWaker`] instance, which defines the\n   382→/// executor-specific wakeup behavior.\n   383→///\n   384→/// The typical life of a `Waker` is that it is constructed by an executor, wrapped in a\n   385→/// [`Context`], then passed to [`Future::poll()`]. Then, if the future chooses to return\n   386→/// [`Poll::Pending`], it must also store the waker somehow and call [`Waker::wake()`] when\n   387→/// the future should be polled again.\n   388→///\n   389→/// Implements [`Clone`], [`Send`], and [`Sync`]; therefore, a waker may be invoked\n   390→/// from any thread, including ones not in any way managed by the executor. For example,\n   391→/// this might be done to wake a future when a blocking function call completes on another\n   392→/// thread.\n   393→///\n   394→/// Note that it is preferable to use `waker.clone_from(&new_waker)` instead\n   395→/// of `*waker = new_waker.clone()`, as the former will avoid cloning the waker\n   396→/// unnecessarily if the two wakers [wake the same task](Self::will_wake).\n   397→///\n   398→/// Constructing a `Waker` from a [`RawWaker`] is unsafe.\n   399→/// Implementing the [`Wake`] trait is a safe alternative that requires memory allocation.\n   400→///\n   401→/// [`Future::poll()`]: core::future::Future::poll\n   402→/// [`Poll::Pending`]: core::task::Poll::Pending\n   403→/// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\n   404→#[repr(transparent)]\n   405→#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   406→#[rustc_diagnostic_item = \"Waker\"]\n   407→pub struct Waker {\n   408→    waker: RawWaker,\n   409→}\n   410→\n   411→#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   412→impl Unpin for Waker {}\n   413→#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   414→unsafe impl Send for Waker {}\n   415→#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   416→unsafe impl Sync for Waker {}\n   417→\n   418→impl Waker {\n   419→    /// Wakes up the task associated with this `Waker`.\n   420→    ///\n   421→    /// As long as the executor keeps running and the task is not finished, it is\n   422→    /// guaranteed that each invocation of [`wake()`](Self::wake) (or\n   423→    /// [`wake_by_ref()`](Self::wake_by_ref)) will be followed by at least one\n   424→    /// [`poll()`] of the task to which this `Waker` belongs. This makes\n   425→    /// it possible to temporarily yield to other tasks while running potentially\n   426→    /// unbounded processing loops.\n   427→    ///\n   428→    /// Note that the above implies that multiple wake-ups may be coalesced into a\n   429→    /// single [`poll()`] invocation by the runtime.\n   430→    ///\n   431→    /// Also note that yielding to competing tasks is not guaranteed: it is the\n   432→    /// executor’s choice which task to run and the executor may choose to run the\n   433→    /// current task again.\n   434→    ///\n   435→    /// [`poll()`]: crate::future::Future::poll\n   436→    #[inline]\n   437→    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   438→    pub fn wake(self) {\n   439→        // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\n   440→        // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\n   441→\n   442→        // Don't call `drop` -- the waker will be consumed by `wake`.\n   443→        let this = ManuallyDrop::new(self);\n   444→\n   445→        // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\n   446→        // to initialize `wake` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\n   447→        // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\n   448→        unsafe { (this.waker.vtable.wake)(this.waker.data) };\n   449→    }\n   450→\n   451→    /// Wakes up the task associated with this `Waker` without consuming the `Waker`.\n   452→    ///\n   453→    /// This is similar to [`wake()`](Self::wake), but may be slightly less efficient in\n   454→    /// the case where an owned `Waker` is available. This method should be preferred to\n   455→    /// calling `waker.clone().wake()`.\n   456→    #[inline]\n   457→    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   458→    pub fn wake_by_ref(&self) {\n   459→        // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\n   460→        // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\n   461→\n   462→        // SAFETY: see `wake`\n   463→        unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.wake_by_ref)(self.waker.data) }\n   464→    }\n   465→\n   466→    /// Returns `true` if this `Waker` and another `Waker` would awake the same task.\n   467→    ///\n   468→    /// This function works on a best-effort basis, and may return false even\n   469→    /// when the `Waker`s would awaken the same task. However, if this function\n   470→    /// returns `true`, it is guaranteed that the `Waker`s will awaken the same task.\n   471→    ///\n   472→    /// This function is primarily used for optimization purposes — for example,\n   473→    /// this type's [`clone_from`](Self::clone_from) implementation uses it to\n   474→    /// avoid cloning the waker when they would wake the same task anyway.\n   475→    #[inline]\n   476→    #[must_use]\n   477→    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   478→    pub fn will_wake(&self, other: &Waker) -> bool {\n   479→        // We optimize this by comparing vtable addresses instead of vtable contents.\n   480→        // This is permitted since the function is documented as best-effort.\n   481→        let RawWaker { data: a_data, vtable: a_vtable } = self.waker;\n   482→        let RawWaker { data: b_data, vtable: b_vtable } = other.waker;\n   483→        a_data == b_data && ptr::eq(a_vtable, b_vtable)\n   484→    }\n   485→\n   486→    /// Creates a new `Waker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\n   487→    ///\n   488→    /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\n   489→    /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\n   490→    /// that is associated with the task.\n   491→    /// The value of this pointer will get passed to all functions that are part\n   492→    /// of the `vtable` as the first parameter.\n   493→    ///\n   494→    /// It is important to consider that the `data` pointer must point to a\n   495→    /// thread safe type such as an `Arc`.\n   496→    ///\n   497→    /// The `vtable` customizes the behavior of a `Waker`. For each operation\n   498→    /// on the `Waker`, the associated function in the `vtable` will be called.\n   499→    ///\n   500→    /// # Safety\n   501→    ///\n   502→    /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\n   503→    /// in [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\n   504→    ///\n   505→    /// (Authors wishing to avoid unsafe code may implement the [`Wake`] trait instead, at the\n   506→    /// cost of a required heap allocation.)\n   507→    ///\n   508→    /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\n   509→    #[inline]\n   510→    #[must_use]\n   511→    #[stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n   512→    #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n   513→    pub const unsafe fn new(data: *const (), vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable) -> Self {\n   514→        Waker { waker: RawWaker { data, vtable } }\n   515→    }\n   516→\n   517→    /// Creates a new `Waker` from [`RawWaker`].\n   518→    ///\n   519→    /// # Safety\n   520→    ///\n   521→    /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\n   522→    /// in [`RawWaker`]'s and [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\n   523→    ///\n   524→    /// (Authors wishing to avoid unsafe code may implement the [`Wake`] trait instead, at the\n   525→    /// cost of a required heap allocation.)\n   526→    ///\n   527→    /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\n   528→    #[inline]\n   529→    #[must_use]\n   530→    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   531→    #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"const_waker\", since = \"1.82.0\")]\n   532→    pub const unsafe fn from_raw(waker: RawWaker) -> Waker {\n   533→        Waker { waker }\n   534→    }\n   535→\n   536→    /// Returns a reference to a `Waker` that does nothing when used.\n   537→    ///\n   538→    // Note!  Much of the documentation for this method is duplicated\n   539→    // in the docs for `LocalWaker::noop`.\n   540→    // If you edit it, consider editing the other copy too.\n   541→    //\n   542→    /// This is mostly useful for writing tests that need a [`Context`] to poll\n   543→    /// some futures, but are not expecting those futures to wake the waker or\n   544→    /// do not need to do anything specific if it happens.\n   545→    ///\n   546→    /// More generally, using `Waker::noop()` to poll a future\n   547→    /// means discarding the notification of when the future should be polled again.\n   548→    /// So it should only be used when such a notification will not be needed to make progress.\n   549→    ///\n   550→    /// If an owned `Waker` is needed, `clone()` this one.\n   551→    ///\n   552→    /// # Examples\n   553→    ///\n   554→    /// ```\n   555→    /// use std::future::Future;\n   556→    /// use std::task;\n   557→    ///\n   558→    /// let mut cx = task::Context::from_waker(task::Waker::noop());\n   559→    ///\n   560→    /// let mut future = Box::pin(async { 10 });\n   561→    /// assert_eq!(future.as_mut().poll(&mut cx), task::Poll::Ready(10));\n   562→    /// ```\n   563→    #[inline]\n   564→    #[must_use]\n   565→    #[stable(feature = \"noop_waker\", since = \"1.85.0\")]\n   566→    #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"noop_waker\", since = \"1.85.0\")]\n   567→    pub const fn noop() -> &'static Waker {\n   568→        const WAKER: &Waker = &Waker { waker: RawWaker::NOOP };\n   569→        WAKER\n   570→    }\n   571→\n   572→    /// Gets the `data` pointer used to create this `Waker`.\n   573→    #[inline]\n   574→    #[must_use]\n   575→    #[stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n   576→    pub fn data(&self) -> *const () {\n   577→        self.waker.data\n   578→    }\n   579→\n   580→    /// Gets the `vtable` pointer used to create this `Waker`.\n   581→    #[inline]\n   582→    #[must_use]\n   583→    #[stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n   584→    pub fn vtable(&self) -> &'static RawWakerVTable {\n   585→        self.waker.vtable\n   586→    }\n   587→\n   588→    /// Constructs a `Waker` from a function pointer.\n   589→    #[inline]\n   590→    #[must_use]\n   591→    #[unstable(feature = \"waker_from_fn_ptr\", issue = \"148457\")]\n   592→    pub const fn from_fn_ptr(f: fn()) -> Self {\n   593→        // SAFETY: Unsafe is used for transmutes, pointer came from `fn()` so it\n   594→        //         is sound to transmute it back to `fn()`.\n   595→        static VTABLE: RawWakerVTable = unsafe {\n   596→            RawWakerVTable::new(\n   597→                |this| RawWaker::new(this, &VTABLE),\n   598→                |this| transmute::<*const (), fn()>(this)(),\n   599→                |this| transmute::<*const (), fn()>(this)(),\n   600→                |_| {},\n   601→            )\n   602→        };\n   603→        let raw = RawWaker::new(f as *const (), &VTABLE);\n   604→\n   605→        // SAFETY: `clone` is just a copy, `drop` is a no-op while `wake` and\n   606→        //         `wake_by_ref` just call the function pointer.\n   607→        unsafe { Self::from_raw(raw) }\n   608→    }\n   609→}\n   610→\n   611→#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   612→impl Clone for Waker {\n   613→    #[inline]\n   614→    fn clone(&self) -> Self {\n   615→        Waker {\n   616→            // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\n   617→            // to initialize `clone` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\n   618→            // that the contract of [`RawWaker`] is upheld.\n   619→            waker: unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.clone)(self.waker.data) },\n   620→        }\n   621→    }\n   622→\n   623→    /// Assigns a clone of `source` to `self`, unless [`self.will_wake(source)`][Waker::will_wake] anyway.\n   624→    ///\n   625→    /// This method is preferred over simply assigning `source.clone()` to `self`,\n   626→    /// as it avoids cloning the waker if `self` is already the same waker.\n   627→    ///\n   628→    /// # Examples\n   629→    ///\n   630→    /// ```\n   631→    /// use std::future::Future;\n   632→    /// use std::pin::Pin;\n   633→    /// use std::sync::{Arc, Mutex};\n   634→    /// use std::task::{Context, Poll, Waker};\n   635→    ///\n   636→    /// struct Waiter {\n   637→    ///     shared: Arc<Mutex<Shared>>,\n   638→    /// }\n   639→    ///\n   640→    /// struct Shared {\n   641→    ///     waker: Waker,\n   642→    ///     // ...\n   643→    /// }\n   644→    ///\n   645→    /// impl Future for Waiter {\n   646→    ///     type Output = ();\n   647→    ///     fn poll(self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<()> {\n   648→    ///         let mut shared = self.shared.lock().unwrap();\n   649→    ///\n   650→    ///         // update the waker\n   651→    ///         shared.waker.clone_from(cx.waker());\n   652→    ///\n   653→    ///         // readiness logic ...\n   654→    /// #       Poll::Ready(())\n   655→    ///     }\n   656→    /// }\n   657→    ///\n   658→    /// ```\n   659→    #[inline]\n   660→    fn clone_from(&mut self, source: &Self) {\n   661→        if !self.will_wake(source) {\n   662→            *self = source.clone();\n   663→        }\n   664→    }\n   665→}\n   666→\n   667→#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   668→impl Drop for Waker {\n   669→    #[inline]\n   670→    fn drop(&mut self) {\n   671→        // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\n   672→        // to initialize `drop` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\n   673→        // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\n   674→        unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.drop)(self.waker.data) }\n   675→    }\n   676→}\n   677→\n   678→#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   679→impl fmt::Debug for Waker {\n   680→    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n   681→        let vtable_ptr = self.waker.vtable as *const RawWakerVTable;\n   682→        f.debug_struct(\"Waker\")\n   683→            .field(\"data\", &self.waker.data)\n   684→            .field(\"vtable\", &vtable_ptr)\n   685→            .finish()\n   686→    }\n   687→}\n   688→\n   689→/// A `LocalWaker` is analogous to a [`Waker`], but it does not implement [`Send`] or [`Sync`].\n   690→///\n   691→/// This handle encapsulates a [`RawWaker`] instance, which defines the\n   692→/// executor-specific wakeup behavior.\n   693→///\n   694→/// Local wakers can be requested from a `Context` with the [`local_waker`] method.\n   695→///\n   696→/// The typical life of a `LocalWaker` is that it is constructed by an executor, wrapped in a\n   697→/// [`Context`] using [`ContextBuilder`], then passed to [`Future::poll()`]. Then, if the future chooses to return\n   698→/// [`Poll::Pending`], it must also store the waker somehow and call [`LocalWaker::wake()`] when\n   699→/// the future should be polled again.\n   700→///\n   701→/// Implements [`Clone`], but neither [`Send`] nor [`Sync`]; therefore, a local waker may\n   702→/// not be moved to other threads. In general, when deciding to use wakers or local wakers,\n   703→/// local wakers are preferable unless the waker needs to be sent across threads. This is because\n   704→/// wakers can incur in additional cost related to memory synchronization.\n   705→///\n   706→/// Note that it is preferable to use `local_waker.clone_from(&new_waker)` instead\n   707→/// of `*local_waker = new_waker.clone()`, as the former will avoid cloning the waker\n   708→/// unnecessarily if the two wakers [wake the same task](Self::will_wake).\n   709→///\n   710→/// # Examples\n   711→/// Usage of a local waker to implement a future analogous to `std::thread::yield_now()`.\n   712→/// ```\n   713→/// #![feature(local_waker)]\n   714→/// use std::future::{Future, poll_fn};\n   715→/// use std::task::Poll;\n   716→///\n   717→/// // a future that returns pending once.\n   718→/// fn yield_now() -> impl Future<Output=()> + Unpin {\n   719→///     let mut yielded = false;\n   720→///     poll_fn(move |cx| {\n   721→///         if !yielded {\n   722→///             yielded = true;\n   723→///             cx.local_waker().wake_by_ref();\n   724→///             return Poll::Pending;\n   725→///         }\n   726→///         return Poll::Ready(())\n   727→///     })\n   728→/// }\n   729→///\n   730→/// # async fn __() {\n   731→/// yield_now().await;\n   732→/// # }\n   733→/// ```\n   734→///\n   735→/// [`Future::poll()`]: core::future::Future::poll\n   736→/// [`Poll::Pending`]: core::task::Poll::Pending\n   737→/// [`local_waker`]: core::task::Context::local_waker\n   738→#[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   739→#[repr(transparent)]\n   740→pub struct LocalWaker {\n   741→    waker: RawWaker,\n   742→}\n   743→\n   744→#[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   745→impl Unpin for LocalWaker {}\n   746→\n   747→impl LocalWaker {\n   748→    /// Wakes up the task associated with this `LocalWaker`.\n   749→    ///\n   750→    /// As long as the executor keeps running and the task is not finished, it is\n   751→    /// guaranteed that each invocation of [`wake()`](Self::wake) (or\n   752→    /// [`wake_by_ref()`](Self::wake_by_ref)) will be followed by at least one\n   753→    /// [`poll()`] of the task to which this `LocalWaker` belongs. This makes\n   754→    /// it possible to temporarily yield to other tasks while running potentially\n   755→    /// unbounded processing loops.\n   756→    ///\n   757→    /// Note that the above implies that multiple wake-ups may be coalesced into a\n   758→    /// single [`poll()`] invocation by the runtime.\n   759→    ///\n   760→    /// Also note that yielding to competing tasks is not guaranteed: it is the\n   761→    /// executor’s choice which task to run and the executor may choose to run the\n   762→    /// current task again.\n   763→    ///\n   764→    /// [`poll()`]: crate::future::Future::poll\n   765→    #[inline]\n   766→    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   767→    pub fn wake(self) {\n   768→        // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\n   769→        // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\n   770→\n   771→        // Don't call `drop` -- the waker will be consumed by `wake`.\n   772→        let this = ManuallyDrop::new(self);\n   773→\n   774→        // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\n   775→        // to initialize `wake` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\n   776→        // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\n   777→        unsafe { (this.waker.vtable.wake)(this.waker.data) };\n   778→    }\n   779→\n   780→    /// Wakes up the task associated with this `LocalWaker` without consuming the `LocalWaker`.\n   781→    ///\n   782→    /// This is similar to [`wake()`](Self::wake), but may be slightly less efficient in\n   783→    /// the case where an owned `Waker` is available. This method should be preferred to\n   784→    /// calling `waker.clone().wake()`.\n   785→    #[inline]\n   786→    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   787→    pub fn wake_by_ref(&self) {\n   788→        // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\n   789→        // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\n   790→\n   791→        // SAFETY: see `wake`\n   792→        unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.wake_by_ref)(self.waker.data) }\n   793→    }\n   794→\n   795→    /// Returns `true` if this `LocalWaker` and another `LocalWaker` would awake the same task.\n   796→    ///\n   797→    /// This function works on a best-effort basis, and may return false even\n   798→    /// when the `Waker`s would awaken the same task. However, if this function\n   799→    /// returns `true`, it is guaranteed that the `Waker`s will awaken the same task.\n   800→    ///\n   801→    /// This function is primarily used for optimization purposes — for example,\n   802→    /// this type's [`clone_from`](Self::clone_from) implementation uses it to\n   803→    /// avoid cloning the waker when they would wake the same task anyway.\n   804→    #[inline]\n   805→    #[must_use]\n   806→    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   807→    pub fn will_wake(&self, other: &LocalWaker) -> bool {\n   808→        // We optimize this by comparing vtable addresses instead of vtable contents.\n   809→        // This is permitted since the function is documented as best-effort.\n   810→        let RawWaker { data: a_data, vtable: a_vtable } = self.waker;\n   811→        let RawWaker { data: b_data, vtable: b_vtable } = other.waker;\n   812→        a_data == b_data && ptr::eq(a_vtable, b_vtable)\n   813→    }\n   814→\n   815→    /// Creates a new `LocalWaker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\n   816→    ///\n   817→    /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\n   818→    /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\n   819→    /// that is associated with the task.\n   820→    /// The value of this pointer will get passed to all functions that are part\n   821→    /// of the `vtable` as the first parameter.\n   822→    ///\n   823→    /// The `vtable` customizes the behavior of a `LocalWaker`. For each\n   824→    /// operation on the `LocalWaker`, the associated function in the `vtable`\n   825→    /// will be called.\n   826→    ///\n   827→    /// # Safety\n   828→    ///\n   829→    /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\n   830→    /// in [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\n   831→    ///\n   832→    #[inline]\n   833→    #[must_use]\n   834→    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   835→    pub const unsafe fn new(data: *const (), vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable) -> Self {\n   836→        LocalWaker { waker: RawWaker { data, vtable } }\n   837→    }\n   838→\n   839→    /// Creates a new `LocalWaker` from [`RawWaker`].\n   840→    ///\n   841→    /// The behavior of the returned `LocalWaker` is undefined if the contract defined\n   842→    /// in [`RawWaker`]'s and [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\n   843→    /// Therefore this method is unsafe.\n   844→    #[inline]\n   845→    #[must_use]\n   846→    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   847→    pub const unsafe fn from_raw(waker: RawWaker) -> LocalWaker {\n   848→        Self { waker }\n   849→    }\n   850→\n   851→    /// Returns a reference to a `LocalWaker` that does nothing when used.\n   852→    ///\n   853→    // Note!  Much of the documentation for this method is duplicated\n   854→    // in the docs for `Waker::noop`.\n   855→    // If you edit it, consider editing the other copy too.\n   856→    //\n   857→    /// This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\n    /// that is associated with the task.\n    /// The value of this field gets passed to all functions that are part of\n    /// the vtable as the first parameter.\n    data: *const (),\n    /// Virtual function pointer table that customizes the behavior of this waker.\n    vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable,\n}\n\nimpl RawWaker {\n    /// Creates a new `RawWaker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\n    ///\n    /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\n    /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\n    /// that is associated with the task.\n    /// The value of this pointer will get passed to all functions that are part\n    /// of the `vtable` as the first parameter.\n    ///\n    /// It is important to consider that the `data` pointer must point to a\n    /// thread safe type such as an `Arc<T: Send + Sync>`\n    /// when used to construct a [`Waker`]. This restriction is lifted when\n    /// constructing a [`LocalWaker`], which allows using types that do not implement\n    /// <code>[Send] + [Sync]</code> like `Rc<T>`.\n    ///\n    /// The `vtable` customizes the behavior of a `Waker` which gets created\n    /// from a `RawWaker`. For each operation on the `Waker`, the associated\n    /// function in the `vtable` of the underlying `RawWaker` will be called.\n    #[inline]\n    #[rustc_promotable]\n    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    #[must_use]\n    pub const fn new(data: *const (), vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable) -> RawWaker {\n        RawWaker { data, vtable }\n    }\n\n    #[stable(feature = \"noop_waker\", since = \"1.85.0\")]\n    const NOOP: RawWaker = {\n        const VTABLE: RawWakerVTable = RawWakerVTable::new(\n            // Cloning just returns a new no-op raw waker\n            |_| RawWaker::NOOP,\n            // `wake` does nothing\n            |_| {},\n            // `wake_by_ref` does nothing\n            |_| {},\n            // Dropping does nothing as we don't allocate anything\n            |_| {},\n        );\n        RawWaker::new(ptr::null(), &VTABLE)\n    };\n}\n\n/// A virtual function pointer table (vtable) that specifies the behavior\n/// of a [`RawWaker`].\n///\n/// The pointer passed to all functions inside the vtable is the `data` pointer\n/// from the enclosing [`RawWaker`] object.\n///\n/// The functions inside this struct are only intended to be called on the `data`\n/// pointer of a properly constructed [`RawWaker`] object from inside the\n/// [`RawWaker`] implementation. Calling one of the contained functions using\n/// any other `data` pointer will cause undefined behavior.\n///\n/// Note that while this type implements `PartialEq`, comparing function pointers, and hence\n/// comparing structs like this that contain function pointers, is unreliable: pointers to the same\n/// function can compare inequal (because functions are duplicated in multiple codegen units), and\n/// pointers to *different* functions can compare equal (since identical functions can be\n/// deduplicated within a codegen unit).\n///\n/// # Thread safety\n/// If the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`Waker`] then\n/// these functions must all be thread-safe (even though [`RawWaker`] is\n/// <code>\\![Send] + \\![Sync]</code>). This is because [`Waker`] is <code>[Send] + [Sync]</code>,\n/// and it may be moved to arbitrary threads or invoked by `&` reference. For example,\n/// this means that if the `clone` and `drop` functions manage a reference count,\n/// they must do so atomically.\n///\n/// However, if the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`LocalWaker`] instead, then\n/// these functions don't need to be thread safe. This means that <code>\\![Send] + \\![Sync]</code>\n///  data can be stored in the data pointer, and reference counting does not need any atomic\n/// synchronization. This is because [`LocalWaker`] is not thread safe itself, so it cannot\n/// be sent across threads.\n#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n#[allow(unpredictable_function_pointer_comparisons)]\n#[derive(PartialEq, Copy, Clone, Debug)]\npub struct RawWakerVTable {\n    /// This function will be called when the [`RawWaker`] gets cloned, e.g. when\n    /// the [`Waker`] in which the [`RawWaker`] is stored gets cloned.\n    ///\n    /// The implementation of this function must retain all resources that are\n    /// required for this additional instance of a [`RawWaker`] and associated\n    /// task. Calling `wake` on the resulting [`RawWaker`] should result in a wakeup\n    /// of the same task that would have been awoken by the original [`RawWaker`].\n    clone: unsafe fn(*const ()) -> RawWaker,\n\n    /// This function will be called when `wake` is called on the [`Waker`].\n    /// It must wake up the task associated with this [`RawWaker`].\n    ///\n    /// The implementation of this function must make sure to release any\n    /// resources that are associated with this instance of a [`RawWaker`] and\n    /// associated task.\n    wake: unsafe fn(*const ()),\n\n    /// This function will be called when `wake_by_ref` is called on the [`Waker`].\n    /// It must wake up the task associated with this [`RawWaker`].\n    ///\n    /// This function is similar to `wake`, but must not consume the provided data\n    /// pointer.\n    wake_by_ref: unsafe fn(*const ()),\n\n    /// This function will be called when a [`Waker`] gets dropped.\n    ///\n    /// The implementation of this function must make sure to release any\n    /// resources that are associated with this instance of a [`RawWaker`] and\n    /// associated task.\n    drop: unsafe fn(*const ()),\n}\n\nimpl RawWakerVTable {\n    /// Creates a new `RawWakerVTable` from the provided `clone`, `wake`,\n    /// `wake_by_ref`, and `drop` functions.\n    ///\n    /// If the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`Waker`] then\n    /// these functions must all be thread-safe (even though [`RawWaker`] is\n    /// <code>\\![Send] + \\![Sync]</code>). This is because [`Waker`] is <code>[Send] + [Sync]</code>,\n    /// and it may be moved to arbitrary threads or invoked by `&` reference. For example,\n    /// this means that if the `clone` and `drop` functions manage a reference count,\n    /// they must do so atomically.\n    ///\n    /// However, if the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`LocalWaker`] instead, then\n    /// these functions don't need to be thread safe. This means that <code>\\![Send] + \\![Sync]</code>\n    /// data can be stored in the data pointer, and reference counting does not need any atomic\n    /// synchronization. This is because [`LocalWaker`] is not thread safe itself, so it cannot\n    /// be sent across threads.\n    /// # `clone`\n    ///\n    /// This function will be called when the [`RawWaker`] gets cloned, e.g. when\n    /// the [`Waker`]/[`LocalWaker`] in which the [`RawWaker`] is stored gets cloned.\n    ///\n    /// The implementation of this function must retain all resources that are\n    /// required for this additional instance of a [`RawWaker`] and associated\n    /// task. Calling `wake` on the resulting [`RawWaker`] should result in a wakeup\n    /// of the same task that would have been awoken by the original [`RawWaker`].\n    ///\n    /// # `wake`\n    ///\n    /// This function will be called when `wake` is called on the [`Waker`].\n    /// It must wake up the task associated with this [`RawWaker`].\n    ///\n    /// The implementation of this function must make sure to release any\n    /// resources that are associated with this instance of a [`RawWaker`] and\n    /// associated task.\n    ///\n    /// # `wake_by_ref`\n    ///\n    /// This function will be called when `wake_by_ref` is called on the [`Waker`].\n    /// It must wake up the task associated with this [`RawWaker`].\n    ///\n    /// This function is similar to `wake`, but must not consume the provided data\n    /// pointer.\n    ///\n    /// # `drop`\n    ///\n    /// This function will be called when a [`Waker`]/[`LocalWaker`] gets\n    /// dropped.\n    ///\n    /// The implementation of this function must make sure to release any\n    /// resources that are associated with this instance of a [`RawWaker`] and\n    /// associated task.\n    #[rustc_promotable]\n    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    pub const fn new(\n        clone: unsafe fn(*const ()) -> RawWaker,\n        wake: unsafe fn(*const ()),\n        wake_by_ref: unsafe fn(*const ()),\n        drop: unsafe fn(*const ()),\n    ) -> Self {\n        Self { clone, wake, wake_by_ref, drop }\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug)]\nenum ExtData<'a> {\n    Some(&'a mut dyn Any),\n    None(()),\n}\n\n/// The context of an asynchronous task.\n///\n/// Currently, `Context` only serves to provide access to a }\n}\n\n/// A Builder used to construct a `Context` instance\n/// with support for `LocalWaker`.\n///\n/// # Examples\n/// ```\n/// #![feature(local_waker)]\n/// use std::task::{ContextBuilder,    Self {\n            waker,\n            local_waker,\n            ext: ExtData::None(()),\n            _marker: PhantomData,\n            _marker2: PhantomData,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Creates a ContextBuilder from an existing Context.\n    #[inline]\n    #[unstable(feature = \"context_ext\", issue = \"123392\")]\n    pub const fn from(cx: &'a mut Context<'_>) -> Self {\n        let ext = #[inline]\n    #[unstable(feature = \"context_ext\", issue = \"123392\")]\n    pub const fn waker(self, waker: &'a Waker) -> Self {\n        Self { waker, ..self }\n    }\n\n    /// Sets the value for AssertUnwindSafe(ext), _marker, _marker2 }\n    }\n}\n\n/// A `Waker` is a handle for waking up a task by notifying its executor that it\n/// is ready to be run.\n///\n/// This handle encapsulates a [`RawWaker`] instance, which defines the\n/// executor-specific wakeup behavior.\n///\n/// The typical life of a `Waker` is that it is constructed by an executor, wrapped in a\n/// [`Context`], then passed to [`Future::poll()`]. Then, if the future chooses to return\n/// [`Poll::Pending`], it must also store the waker somehow and call [`Waker::wake()`] when\n/// the future should be polled again.\n///\n/// Implements [`Clone`], [`Send`], and [`Sync`]; therefore, a waker may be invoked\n/// from any thread, including ones not in any way managed by the executor. For example,\n/// this might be done to wake a future when a blocking function call completes on another\n/// thread.\n///\n/// Note that it is preferable to use `waker.clone_from(&new_waker)` instead\n/// of `*waker = new_waker.clone()`, as the former will avoid cloning the waker\n/// unnecessarily if the two wakers [wake the same task](Self::will_wake).\n///\n/// Constructing a `Waker` from a [`RawWaker`] is unsafe.\n/// Implementing the [`Wake`] trait is a safe alternative that requires memory allocation.\n///\n/// [`Future::poll()`]: core::future::Future::poll\n/// [`Poll::Pending`]: core::task::Poll::Pending\n/// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\n#[repr(transparent)]\n#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n#[rustc_diagnostic_item = \"Waker\"]\npub struct Waker {\n    waker: RawWaker,\n}\n\n#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\nimpl Unpin for Waker {}\n#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\nunsafe impl Send for Waker {}\n#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\nunsafe impl Sync for Waker {}\n\nimpl Waker {\n    /// Wakes up the task associated with this `Waker`.\n    ///\n    /// As long as the executor keeps running and the task is not finished, it is\n    /// guaranteed that each invocation of [`wake()`](Self::wake) (or\n    /// [`wake_by_ref()`](Self::wake_by_ref)) will be followed by at least one\n    /// [`poll()`] of the task to which this `Waker` belongs. This makes\n    /// it possible to temporarily yield to other tasks while running potentially\n    /// unbounded processing loops.\n    ///\n    /// Note that the above implies that multiple wake-ups may be coalesced into a\n    /// single [`poll()`] invocation by the runtime.\n    ///\n    /// Also note that yielding to competing tasks is not guaranteed: it is the\n    /// executor’s choice which task to run and the executor may choose to run the\n    /// current task again.\n    ///\n    /// [`poll()`]: crate::future::Future::poll\n    #[inline]\n    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    pub fn wake(self) {\n        // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\n        // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\n\n        // Don't call `drop` -- the waker will be consumed by `wake`.\n        let this = ManuallyDrop::new(self);\n\n        // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\n        // to initialize `wake` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\n        // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\n        unsafe { (this.waker.vtable.wake)(this.waker.data) };\n    }\n\n    /// Wakes up the task associated with this `Waker` without consuming the `Waker`.\n    ///\n    /// This is similar to [`wake()`](Self::wake), but may be slightly less efficient in\n    /// the case where an owned `Waker` is available. For each operation\n    /// on the `Waker`, the associated function in the `vtable` will be called.\n    ///\n    /// # Safety\n    ///\n    /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\n    /// in [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\n    ///\n    /// (Authors wishing to avoid unsafe code may implement the [`Wake`] trait instead, at the\n    /// cost of a required heap allocation.)\n    ///\n    /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\n    #[inline]\n    #[must_use]\n    #[stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n    #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n    pub const unsafe fn new(data: *const (), vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable) -> Self {\n        Waker { waker: RawWaker { data, vtable } }\n    }\n\n    /// Creates a new `Waker` from [`RawWaker`].\n    ///\n    /// # Safety\n    ///\n    /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\n    /// in [`RawWaker`]'s and [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\n    ///\n    /// (Authors wishing to avoid unsafe code may implement the [`Wake`] trait instead, at the\n    /// cost of a required heap allocation.)\n    ///\n    /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\n    #[inline]\n    #[must_use]\n    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"const_waker\", since = \"1.82.0\")]\n    pub const unsafe fn from_raw(waker: RawWaker) -> Waker {\n        Waker { waker }\n    }\n\n    /// Returns a reference to a `Waker` that does nothing when used.\n    ///\n    // Note! This kind of\n/// \"asynchronous value\" makes it possible for a thread to continue doing useful\n/// work while it waits for the value to become available.\n///\n/// # The `poll` method\n///\n/// The core method of future, `poll`, *attempts* to resolve the future into a\n/// final value. This method does not block if the value is not ready. Instead,\n/// the current task is scheduled to be woken up when it's possible to make\n/// further progress by `poll`ing again. The `context` passed to the `poll`\n/// method can provide a [`Waker`], which is a handle for waking up the current\n/// task.\n///\n/// When using a future, you generally won't call `poll` directly, but instead\n/// `.await` the value.\n///\n/// [`async`]: ../../std/keyword.async.html\n/// [`Waker`]: crate::task::Waker\n#[doc(notable_trait)]\n#[doc(search_unbox)]\n#[must_use = \"futures do nothing unless you `.await` or poll them\"]\n#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n#[lang = \"future_trait\"]\n#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented(\n    label = \"`{Self}` is not a future\",\n    message = \"`{Self}` is not a future\"\n)]\npub trait Future {\n    /// The type of value produced on completion.\n    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    #[lang = \"future_output\"]\n    type Output;\n\n    /// Attempts to resolve the future to a final value, registering\n    /// the current task for wakeup if the value is not yet available.\n    ///\n    /// # Return value\n    ///\n    /// This function returns:\n    ///\n    /// - [`Poll::Pending`] if the future is not ready yet\n    /// - [`Poll::Ready(val)`] with the result `val` of this future if it\n    ///   finished successfully.\n    ///\n    /// Once a future has finished, clients should not `poll` it again.\n    ///\n    /// When a future is not ready yet, `poll` returns `Poll::Pending` and\n    /// stores a clone of the [`Waker`] copied from the current [`Context`].\n    /// This [`Waker`] is then woken once the future can make progress.\n    /// For example, a future waiting for a socket to become\n    /// readable would call `.clone()` on the [`Waker`] and store it.\n    /// When a signal arrives elsewhere indicating that the socket is readable,\n    /// [`Waker::wake`] is called and the socket future's task is awoken.\n    /// Once a task has been woken up, it should attempt to `poll` the future\n    /// again, which may or may not produce a final value.\n    ///\n    /// Note that on multiple calls to `poll`, only the [`Waker`] from the\n    /// [`Context`] passed to the most recent call should be scheduled to\n    /// receive a wakeup.\n    ///\n    /// # Runtime characteristics\n    ///\n    /// Futures alone are *inert*; they must be *actively* `poll`ed for the\n    /// underlying computation to make progress, meaning that each time the\n    /// current task is woken up, it should actively re-`poll` pending futures\n    /// that it still has an interest in.\n    ///\n    /// Having said that, some Futures may represent a value that is being\n    /// computed in a different task. In this case, the future's underlying\n    /// computation is simply acting as a conduit for a value being computed\n    /// by that other task, which will proceed independently of the Future.\n    /// Futures of this kind are typically obtained when spawning a new task into an\n    /// async runtime.\n    ///\n    /// The `poll` function should not be called repeatedly in a tight loop --\n    /// instead, it should only be called when the future indicates that it is\n    /// ready to make progress (by calling `wake()`). If you're familiar with the\n    /// `poll(2)` or `select(2)` syscalls on Unix it's worth noting that futures\n    /// typically do *not* suffer the same problems of \"all wakeups must poll\n    /// all events\"; they are more like `epoll(4)`.\n    ///\n    /// An implementation of `poll` should strive to return quickly, and should\n    /// not block. Returning quickly prevents unnecessarily clogging up\n    /// threads or event loops. If it is known ahead of time that a call to\n    /// `poll` may end up taking a while, the work should be offloaded to a\n    /// thread pool (or something similar) to ensure that `poll` can return\n    /// quickly.\n    ///\n    /// # Panics\n    ///\n    /// Once a future has completed (returned `Ready` from `poll`), calling its\n    /// `poll` method again may panic, block forever, or cause other kinds of\n    /// problems; the `Future` trait places no requirements on the effects of\n    /// such a call. However, as the `poll` method is not marked `unsafe`,\n    /// Rust's usual rules apply: calls must never cause undefined behavior\n    /// (memory corruption, incorrect use of `unsafe` functions, or the like),\n    /// regardless of the future's state.\n    ///\n    /// [`Poll::Ready(val)`]: Poll::Ready\n    /// [`Waker`]: crate::task::Waker\n    /// [`Waker::wake`]: crate::task::Waker::wake\n    #[lang = \"poll\"]\n    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    fn poll(self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<Self::Output>;\n}\n\n#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\nimpl<F: ?Sized + Future + Unpin> Future for &mut F {\n    type Output = F::Output;\n\n    fn poll(mut self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<Self::Output> {\n        F::poll(Pin::new(&mut **self), cx)\n    }\n}\n\n#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\nimpl<P> Future for Pin<P>\nwhere\n    P: ops::DerefMut<Target: Future>,\n{\n    type Output = <<P as ops::Deref>::Target as Future>::Output;\n\n    fn poll(self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<Self::Output> {\n        <P::Target as Future>::poll(self.as_deref_mut(), cx)\n    }\n}\n","numLines":136,"startLine":1,"totalLines":136}}}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_0121PoyFfK3krsGbzHkoUz6b","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→#![stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\n     2→\n     3→//! Types and Traits for working with asynchronous tasks.\n     4→//!\n     5→//! **Note**: Some of the types in this module are only available\n     6→//! on platforms that support atomic loads and stores of pointers.\n     7→//! This may be detected at compile time using\n     8→//! `#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]`.\n     9→\n    10→use core::mem::ManuallyDrop;\n    11→#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n    12→use core::task::Waker;\n    13→use core::task::{LocalWaker, RawWaker, RawWakerVTable};\n    14→\n    15→use crate::rc::Rc;\n    16→#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n    17→use crate::sync::Arc;\n    18→\n    19→/// The implementation of waking a task on an executor.\n    20→///\n    21→/// This trait can be used to create a [`Waker`]. An executor can define an\n    22→/// implementation of this trait, and use that to construct a [`Waker`] to pass\n    23→/// to the tasks that are executed on that executor.\n    24→///\n    25→/// This trait is a memory-safe and ergonomic alternative to constructing a\n    26→/// [`RawWaker`]. It supports the common executor design in which the data used\n    27→/// to wake up a task is stored in an [`Arc`]. Some executors (especially\n    28→/// those for embedded systems) cannot use this API, which is why [`RawWaker`]\n    29→/// exists as an alternative for those systems.\n    30→///\n    31→/// To construct a [`Waker`] from some type `W` implementing this trait,\n    32→/// wrap it in an [`Arc<W>`](Arc) and call `Waker::from()` on that.\n    33→/// It is also possible to convert to [`RawWaker`] in the same way.\n    34→///\n    35→/// <!-- Ideally we'd link to the `From` impl, but rustdoc doesn't generate any page for it within\n    36→///      `alloc` because `alloc` neither defines nor re-exports `From` or `Waker`, and we can't\n    37→///      link ../../std/task/struct.Waker.html#impl-From%3CArc%3CW,+Global%3E%3E-for-Waker\n    38→///      without getting a link-checking error in CI. -->\n    39→///\n    40→/// # Examples\n    41→///\n    42→/// A basic `block_on` function that takes a future and runs it to completion on\n    43→/// the current thread.\n    44→///\n    45→/// **Note:** This example trades correctness for simplicity. In order to prevent\n    46→/// deadlocks, production-grade implementations will also need to handle\n    47→/// intermediate calls to `thread::unpark` as well as nested invocations.\n    48→///\n    49→/// ```rust\n    50→/// use std::future::Future;\n    51→/// use std::sync::Arc;\n    52→/// use std::task::{Context, Poll, Wake};\n    53→/// use std::thread::{self, Thread};\n    54→/// use core::pin::pin;\n    55→///\n    56→/// /// A waker that wakes up the current thread when called.\n    57→/// struct ThreadWaker(Thread);\n    58→///\n    59→/// impl Wake for ThreadWaker {\n    60→///     fn wake(self: Arc<Self>) {\n    61→///         self.0.unpark();\n    62→///     }\n    63→/// }\n    64→///\n    65→/// /// Run a future to completion on the current thread.\n    66→/// fn block_on<T>(fut: impl Future<Output = T>) -> T {\n    67→///     // Pin the future so it can be polled.\n    68→///     let mut fut = pin!(fut);\n    69→///\n    70→///     // Create a new context to be passed to the future.\n    71→///     let t = thread::current();\n    72→///     let waker = Arc::new(ThreadWaker(t)).into();\n    73→///     let mut cx = Context::from_waker(&waker);\n    74→///\n    75→///     // Run the future to completion.\n    76→///     loop {\n    77→///         match fut.as_mut().poll(&mut cx) {\n    78→///             Poll::Ready(res) => return res,\n    79→///             Poll::Pending => thread::park(),\n    80→///         }\n    81→///     }\n    82→/// }\n    83→///\n    84→/// block_on(async {\n    85→///     println!(\"Hi from inside a future!\");\n    86→/// });\n    87→/// ```\n    88→#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n    89→#[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\n    90→pub trait Wake {\n    91→    /// Wake this task.\n    92→    #[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\n    93→    fn wake(self: Arc<Self>);\n    94→\n    95→    /// Wake this task without consuming the waker.\n    96→    ///\n    97→    /// If an By default, it clones the\n    99→    /// [`Arc`] and calls [`wake`] on the clone.\n   100→    ///\n   101→    /// [`wake`]: Wake::wake\n   102→    #[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\n   109→impl<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static> From<Arc<W>> for Waker {\n   110→    /// Use a [`Wake`]-able type as a `Waker`.\n   111→    ///\n   112→    /// No      // a RawWaker from Arc<W>.\n   116→        unsafe { Waker::from_raw(raw_waker(waker)) }\n   117→    }\n   118→}\n   119→#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n   120→#[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\n   121→impl<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static> From<Arc<W>> for RawWaker {\n   122→    /// Use a `Wake`-able type as a `RawWaker`.\n   123→    ///\n   124→    /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\n   125→    fn from(waker: Arc<W>) -> RawWaker {\n   126→        raw_waker(waker)\n   127→    }\n   128→}\n   129→\n   130→// NB: This private function for constructing a RawWaker is used, rather than\n   131→// inlining this into the `From<Arc<W>> for RawWaker` impl, to ensure that\n   132→// the safety of `From<Arc<W>> for Waker` does not depend on the correct\n   133→// trait dispatch - instead both impls call this function directly and\n   134→// explicitly.\n   135→#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n   136→#[inline(always)]\n   137→fn raw_waker<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: Arc<W>) -> RawWaker {\n   138→    // Increment the reference count of the arc to clone it.\n   139→    //\n   140→    // The #[inline(always)] is to ensure that raw_waker and clone_waker are\n   141→    // always generated in the same code generation unit as one another, and\n   142→    // therefore that the structurally identical const-promoted RawWakerVTable\n   143→    // within both functions is deduplicated at LLVM IR code generation time.\n   144→    // This allows optimizing Waker::will_wake to a single pointer comparison of\n   145→    // the vtable pointers, rather than comparing all four function pointers\n   146→    // within the vtables.\n   147→    #[inline(always)]\n   148→    unsafe fn clone_waker<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) -> RawWaker {\n   149→        unsafe { Arc::increment_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\n   150→        RawWaker::new(\n   151→            waker,\n   152→            &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\n   153→        )\n   154→    }\n   155→\n   156→    // Wake by value, moving the Arc into the Wake::wake function\n   157→    unsafe fn wake<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n   158→        let waker = unsafe { Arc::from_raw(waker as *const W) };\n   159→        <W as Wake>::wake(waker);\n   160→    }\n   161→\n   162→    // Wake by reference, wrap the waker in ManuallyDrop to avoid dropping it\n   163→    unsafe fn wake_by_ref<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n   164→        let waker = unsafe { ManuallyDrop::new(Arc::from_raw(waker as *const W)) };\n   165→        <W as Wake>::wake_by_ref(&waker);\n   166→    }\n   167→\n   168→    // Decrement the reference count of the Arc on drop\n   169→    unsafe fn drop_waker<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n   170→        unsafe { Arc::decrement_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\n   171→    }\n   172→\n   173→    RawWaker::new(\n   174→        Arc::into_raw(waker) as *const (),\n   175→        &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\n   176→    )\n   177→}\n   178→\n   179→/// An analogous trait to `Wake` but used to construct a `LocalWaker`.\n   180→///\n   181→/// This API works in exactly the same way as `Wake`,\n   182→/// except that it uses an `Rc` instead of an `Arc`,\n   183→/// and the result is a `LocalWaker` instead of a `Waker`.\n   184→///\n   185→/// The benefits of using `LocalWaker` over `Waker` are that it allows the local waker\n   186→/// to hold data that does not implement `Send` and `Sync`. Additionally, it saves calls\n   187→/// to `Arc::clone`, which requires atomic synchronization.\n   188→///\n   189→///\n   190→/// # Examples\n   191→///\n   192→/// This is a simplified example of a `spawn` and a `block_on` function. The `spawn` function\n   193→/// is used to push new tasks onto the run queue, while the block on function will remove them\n   194→/// and poll them. When a task is woken, it will put itself back on the run queue to be polled\n   195→/// by the executor.\n   196→///\n   197→/// **Note:** This example trades correctness for simplicity. A real world example would interleave\n   198→/// poll calls with calls to an io reactor to wait for events instead of spinning on a loop.\n   199→///\n   200→/// ```rust\n   201→/// #![feature(local_waker)]\n   202→/// use std::task::{LocalWake, ContextBuilder, LocalWaker, Waker};\n   203→/// use std::future::Future;\n   204→/// use std::pin::Pin;\n   205→/// use std::rc::Rc;\n   206→/// use std::cell::RefCell;\n   207→/// use std::collections::VecDeque;\n   208→///\n   209→///\n   210→/// thread_local! {\n   211→///     // A queue containing all tasks ready to do progress\n   212→///     static RUN_QUEUE: RefCell<VecDeque<Rc<Task>>> = RefCell::default();\n   213→/// }\n   214→///\n   215→/// type BoxedFuture = Pin<Box<dyn Future<Output = ()>>>;\n   216→///\n   217→/// struct Task(RefCell<BoxedFuture>);\n   218→///\n   219→/// impl LocalWake for Task {\n   220→///     fn wake(self: Rc<Self>) {\n   221→///         RUN_QUEUE.with_borrow_mut(|queue| {\n   222→///             queue.push_back(self)\n   223→///         })\n   224→///     }\n   225→/// }\n   226→///\n   227→/// fn spawn<F>(future: F)\n   228→/// where\n   229→///     F: Future<Output=()> + 'static + Send + Sync\n   230→/// {\n   231→///     let task = RefCell::new(Box::pin(future));\n   232→///     RUN_QUEUE.with_borrow_mut(|queue| {\n   233→///         queue.push_back(Rc::new(Task(task)));\n   234→///     });\n   235→/// }\n   236→///\n   237→/// fn block_on<F>(future: F)\n   238→/// where\n   239→///     F: Future<Output=()> + 'static + Sync + Send\n   240→/// {\n   241→///     spawn(future);\n   242→///     loop {\n   243→///         let Some(task) = RUN_QUEUE.with_borrow_mut(|queue| queue.pop_front()) else {\n   244→///             // we exit, since there are no more tasks remaining on the queue\n   245→///             return;\n   246→///         };\n   247→///\n   248→///         // cast the Rc<Task> into a `LocalWaker`\n   249→///         let local_waker: LocalWaker = task.clone().into();\n   250→///         // Build the context using `ContextBuilder`\n   251→///         let mut cx = ContextBuilder::from_waker(Waker::noop())\n   252→///             .local_waker(&local_waker)\n   253→///             .build();\n   254→///\n   255→///         // Poll the task\n   256→///         let _ = task.0\n   257→///             .borrow_mut()\n   258→///             .as_mut()\n   259→///             .poll(&mut cx);\n   260→///     }\n   261→/// }\n   262→///\n   263→/// block_on(async {\n   264→///     println!(\"hello world\");\n   265→/// });\n   266→/// ```\n   267→///\n   268→#[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   269→pub trait LocalWake {\n   270→    /// Wake this task.\n   271→    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue By default, it clones the\n   278→    /// [`Rc`] and calls [`wake`] on the clone.\n   279→    ///\n   280→    /// [`wake`]: LocalWaker::wake\n   281→    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   282→    fn wake_by_ref(self: &Rc<Self>) {\n   283→        self.clone().wake();\n   284→    }\n   285→}\n   286→\n   287→#[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   288→impl<W: LocalWake + 'static> From<Rc<W>> for LocalWaker {\n   289→    /// Use a `Wake`-able type as a `LocalWaker`.\n   290→    ///\n   291→    /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\n   292→    fn from(waker: Rc<W>) -> LocalWaker {\n   293→        // SAFETY: This is safe because raw_waker safely constructs\n   294→        // a RawWaker from Rc<W>.\n   295→        unsafe { LocalWaker::from_raw(local_raw_waker(waker)) }\n   296→    }\n   297→}\n   298→#[allow(ineffective_unstable_trait_impl)]\n   299→#[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   300→impl<W: LocalWake + 'static> From<Rc<W>> for RawWaker {\n   301→    /// Use a `Wake`-able type as a `RawWaker`.\n   302→    ///\n   303→    /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\n   304→    fn from(waker: Rc<W>) -> RawWaker {\n   305→        local_raw_waker(waker)\n   306→    }\n   307→}\n   308→\n   309→// NB: This private function for constructing a RawWaker is used, rather than\n   310→// inlining this into the `From<Rc<W>> for RawWaker` impl, to ensure that\n   311→// the safety of `From<Rc<W>> for Waker` does not depend on the correct\n   312→// trait dispatch - instead both impls call this function directly and\n   313→// explicitly.\n   314→#[inline(always)]\n   315→fn local_raw_waker<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: Rc<W>) -> RawWaker {\n   316→    // Increment the reference count of the Rc to clone it.\n   317→    //\n   318→    // Refer to the comment on raw_waker's clone_waker regarding why this is\n   319→    // always inline.\n   320→    #[inline(always)]\n   321→    unsafe fn clone_waker<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: *const ()) -> RawWaker {\n   322→        unsafe { Rc::increment_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\n   323→        RawWaker::new(\n   324→            waker,\n   325→            &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\n   326→        )\n   327→    }\n   328→\n   329→    // Wake by value, moving the Rc into the LocalWake::wake function\n   330→    unsafe fn wake<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n   331→        let waker = unsafe { Rc::from_raw(waker as *const W) };\n   332→        <W as LocalWake>::wake(waker);\n   333→    }\n   334→\n   335→    // Wake by reference, wrap the waker in ManuallyDrop to avoid dropping it\n   336→    unsafe fn wake_by_ref<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n   337→        let waker = unsafe { ManuallyDrop::new(Rc::from_raw(waker as *const W)) };\n   338→        <W as LocalWake>::wake_by_ref(&waker);\n   339→    }\n   340→\n   341→    // Decrement the reference count of the Rc on drop\n   342→    unsafe fn drop_waker<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n   343→        unsafe { Rc::decrement_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\n   344→    }\n   345→\n   346→    RawWaker::new(\n   347→        Rc::into_raw(waker) as *const (),\n   348→        &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\n   349→    )\n   350→}\n   351→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Types and Traits for working with asynchronous tasks.\n//!\n//! **Note**: Some of the types in this module are only available\n//! on platforms that support atomic loads and stores of pointers.\n//! This may be detected at compile time using\n//! `#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]`.\n\nuse core::mem::ManuallyDrop;\n#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\nuse core::task::Waker;\nuse core::task::{LocalWaker, RawWaker, RawWakerVTable};\n\nuse crate::rc::Rc;\n#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\nuse crate::sync::Arc;\n\n/// The implementation of waking a task on an executor.\n///\n/// This trait can be used to create a [`Waker`]. An executor can define an\n/// implementation of this trait, and use that to construct a [`Waker`] to pass\n/// to the tasks that are executed on that executor.\n///\n/// This trait is a memory-safe and ergonomic alternative to constructing a\n/// [`RawWaker`]. It supports the common executor design in which the data used\n/// to wake up a task is stored in an [`Arc`]. Some executors (especially\n/// those for embedded systems) cannot use this API, which is why [`RawWaker`]\n/// exists as an alternative for those systems.\n///\n/// To construct a [`Waker`] from some type `W` implementing this trait,\n/// wrap it in an [`Arc<W>`](Arc) and call `Waker::from()` on that.\n/// It is also possible to convert to [`RawWaker`] in the same way.\n///\n/// <!-- Ideally we'd link to the `From` impl, but rustdoc doesn't generate any page for it within\n///      `alloc` because `alloc` neither defines nor re-exports `From` or `Waker`, and we can't\n///      link ../../std/task/struct.Waker.html#impl-From%3CArc%3CW,+Global%3E%3E-for-Waker\n///      without getting a link-checking error in CI. -->\n///\n/// # Examples\n///\n/// A basic `block_on` function that takes a future and runs it to completion on\n/// the current thread.\n///\n/// **Note:** This example trades correctness for simplicity. In order to prevent\n/// deadlocks, production-grade implementations will also need to handle\n/// intermediate calls to `thread::unpark` as well as nested invocations.\n///\n/// ```rust\n/// use std::future::Future;\n/// use std::sync::Arc;\n/// use std::task::{Context, Poll, Wake};\n/// use std::thread::{self, Thread};\n/// use core::pin::pin;\n///\n/// /// A waker that wakes up the current thread when called.\n/// struct ThreadWaker(Thread);\n///\n/// impl Wake for ThreadWaker {\n///     fn wake(self: Arc<Self>) {\n///         self.0.unpark();\n///     }\n/// }\n///\n/// /// Run a future to completion on the current thread.\n/// fn block_on<T>(fut: impl Future<Output = T>) -> T {\n///     // Pin the future so it can be polled.\n///     let mut fut = pin!(fut);\n///\n///     // Create a new context to be passed to the future.\n///     let t = thread::current();\n///     let waker = Arc::new(ThreadWaker(t)).into();\n///     let mut cx = Context::from_waker(&waker);\n///\n///     // Run the future to completion.\n///     loop {\n///         match fut.as_mut().poll(&mut cx) {\n///             Poll::Ready(res) => return res,\n///             Poll::Pending => thread::park(),\n///         }\n///     }\n/// }\n///\n/// block_on(async {\n///     println!(\"Hi from inside a future!\");\n/// });\n/// ```\n#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n#[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\npub trait Wake {\n    /// Wake this task.\n    #[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\n    fn wake(self: Arc<Self>);\n\n    /// Wake this task without consuming the waker.\n    ///\n    /// If an executor supports a cheaper way to wake without consuming the\n    /// waker, it should override this method. By default, it clones the\n    /// [`Arc`] and calls [`wake`] on the clone.\n    ///\n    /// [`wake`]: Wake::wake\n    #[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\n    fn wake_by_ref(self: &Arc<Self>) {\n        self.clone().wake();\n    }\n}\n#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n#[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\nimpl<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static> From<Arc<W>> for Waker {\n    /// Use a [`Wake`]-able type as a `Waker`.\n    ///\n    /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\n    fn from(waker: Arc<W>) -> Waker {\n        // SAFETY: This is safe because raw_waker safely constructs\n        // a RawWaker from Arc<W>.\n        unsafe { Waker::from_raw(raw_waker(waker)) }\n    }\n}\n#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n#[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\nimpl<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static> From<Arc<W>> for RawWaker {\n    /// Use a `Wake`-able type as a `RawWaker`.\n    ///\n    /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\n    fn from(waker: Arc<W>) -> RawWaker {\n        raw_waker(waker)\n    }\n}\n\n// NB: This private function for constructing a RawWaker is used, rather than\n// inlining this into the `From<Arc<W>> for RawWaker` impl, to ensure that\n// the safety of `From<Arc<W>> for Waker` does not depend on the correct\n// trait dispatch - instead both impls call this function directly and\n// explicitly.\n#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n#[inline(always)]\nfn raw_waker<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: Arc<W>) -> RawWaker {\n    // Increment the reference count of the arc to clone it.\n    //\n    // The #[inline(always)] is to ensure that raw_waker and clone_waker are\n    // always generated in the same code generation unit as one another, and\n    // therefore that the structurally identical const-promoted RawWakerVTable\n    // within both functions is deduplicated at LLVM IR code generation time.\n    // This allows optimizing Waker::will_wake to a single pointer comparison of\n    // the vtable pointers, rather than comparing all four function pointers\n    // within the vtables.\n    #[inline(always)]\n    unsafe fn clone_waker<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) -> RawWaker {\n        unsafe { Arc::increment_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\n        RawWaker::new(\n            waker,\n            &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\n        )\n    }\n\n    // Wake by value, moving the Arc into the Wake::wake function\n    unsafe fn wake<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n        let waker = unsafe { Arc::from_raw(waker as *const W) };\n        <W as Wake>::wake(waker);\n    }\n\n    // Wake by reference, wrap the waker in ManuallyDrop to avoid dropping it\n    unsafe fn wake_by_ref<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n        let waker = unsafe { ManuallyDrop::new(Arc::from_raw(waker as *const W)) };\n        <W as Wake>::wake_by_ref(&waker);\n    }\n\n    // Decrement the reference count of the Arc on drop\n    unsafe fn drop_waker<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n        unsafe { Arc::decrement_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\n    }\n\n    RawWaker::new(\n        Arc::into_raw(waker) as *const (),\n        &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\n    )\n}\n\n/// An analogous trait to `Wake` but used to construct a `LocalWaker`.\n///\n/// This API works in exactly the same way as `Wake`,\n/// except that it uses an `Rc` instead of an `Arc`,\n/// and the result is a `LocalWaker` instead of a `Waker`.\n///\n/// The benefits of using `LocalWaker` over `Waker` are that it allows the local waker\n/// to hold data that does not implement `Send` and `Sync`. Additionally, it saves calls\n/// to `Arc::clone`, which requires atomic synchronization.\n///\n///\n/// # Examples\n///\n/// This is a simplified example of a `spawn` and a `block_on` function. The `spawn` function\n/// is used to push new tasks onto the run queue, while the block on function will remove them\n/// and poll them. When a task is woken, it will put itself back on the run queue to be polled\n/// by the executor.\n///\n/// **Note:** This example trades correctness for simplicity. A real world example would interleave\n/// poll calls with calls to an io reactor to wait for events instead of spinning on a loop.\n///\n/// ```rust\n/// #![feature(local_waker)]\n/// use std::task::{LocalWake, ContextBuilder, LocalWaker, Waker};\n/// use std::future::Future;\n/// use std::pin::Pin;\n/// use std::rc::Rc;\n/// use std::cell::RefCell;\n/// use std::collections::VecDeque;\n///\n///\n/// thread_local! {\n///     // A queue containing all tasks ready to do progress\n///     static RUN_QUEUE: RefCell<VecDeque<Rc<Task>>> = RefCell::default();\n/// }\n///\n/// type BoxedFuture = Pin<Box<dyn Future<Output = ()>>>;\n///\n/// struct Task(RefCell<BoxedFuture>);\n///\n/// impl LocalWake for Task {\n///     fn wake(self: Rc<Self>) {\n///         RUN_QUEUE.with_borrow_mut(|queue| {\n///             queue.push_back(self)\n///         })\n///     }\n/// }\n///\n/// fn spawn<F>(future: F)\n/// where\n///     F: Future<Output=()> + 'static + Send + Sync\n/// {\n///     let task = RefCell::new(Box::pin(future));\n///     RUN_QUEUE.with_borrow_mut(|queue| {\n///         queue.push_back(Rc::new(Task(task)));\n///     });\n/// }\n///\n/// fn block_on<F>(future: F)\n/// where\n///     F: Future<Output=()> + 'static + Sync + Send\n/// {\n///     spawn(future);\n///     loop {\n///         let Some(task) = RUN_QUEUE.with_borrow_mut(|queue| queue.pop_front()) else {\n///             // we exit, since there are no more tasks remaining on the queue\n///             return;\n///         };\n///\n///         // cast the Rc<Task> into a `LocalWaker`\n///         let local_waker: LocalWaker = task.clone().into();\n///         // Build the context using `ContextBuilder`\n///         let mut cx = ContextBuilder::from_waker(Waker::noop())\n///             .local_waker(&local_waker)\n///             .build();\n///\n///         // Poll the task\n///         let _ = task.0\n///             .borrow_mut()\n///             .as_mut()\n///             .poll(&mut cx);\n///     }\n/// }\n///\n/// block_on(async {\n///     println!(\"hello world\");\n/// });\n/// ```\n///\n#[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\npub trait LocalWake {\n    /// Wake this task.\n    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n    fn wake(self: Rc<Self>);\n\n    /// Wake this task without consuming the local waker.\n    ///\n    /// If an executor supports a cheaper way to wake without consuming the\n    /// waker, it should override this method. By default, it clones the\n    /// [`Rc`] and calls [`wake`] on the clone.\n    ///\n    /// [`wake`]: LocalWaker::wake\n    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n    fn wake_by_ref(self: &Rc<Self>) {\n        self.clone().wake();\n    }\n}\n\n#[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\nimpl<W: LocalWake + 'static> From<Rc<W>> for LocalWaker {\n    /// Use a `Wake`-able type as a `LocalWaker`.\n    ///\n    /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\n    fn from(waker: Rc<W>) -> LocalWaker {\n        // SAFETY: This is safe because raw_waker safely constructs\n        // a RawWaker from Rc<W>.\n        unsafe { LocalWaker::from_raw(local_raw_waker(waker)) }\n    }\n}\n#[allow(ineffective_unstable_trait_impl)]\n#[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\nimpl<W: LocalWake + 'static> From<Rc<W>> for RawWaker {\n    /// Use a `Wake`-able type as a `RawWaker`.\n    ///\n    /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\n    fn from(waker: Rc<W>) -> RawWaker {\n        local_raw_waker(waker)\n    }\n}\n\n// NB: This private function for constructing a RawWaker is used, rather than\n// inlining this into the `From<Rc<W>> for RawWaker` impl, to ensure that\n// the safety of `From<Rc<W>> for Waker` does not depend on the correct\n// trait dispatch - instead both impls call this function directly and\n// explicitly.\n#[inline(always)]\nfn local_raw_waker<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: Rc<W>) -> RawWaker {\n    // Increment the reference count of the Rc to clone it.\n    //\n    // Refer to the comment on raw_waker's clone_waker regarding why this is\n    // always inline.\n    #[inline(always)]\n    unsafe fn clone_waker<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: *const ()) -> RawWaker {\n        unsafe { Rc::increment_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\n        RawWaker::new(\n            waker,\n            &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\n        )\n    }\n\n    // Wake by value, moving the Rc into the LocalWake::wake function\n    unsafe fn wake<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n        let waker = unsafe { Rc::from_raw(waker as *const W) };\n        <W as LocalWake>::wake(waker);\n    }\n\n    // Wake by reference, wrap the waker in ManuallyDrop to avoid dropping it\n    unsafe fn wake_by_ref<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n        let waker = unsafe { ManuallyDrop::new(Rc::from_raw(waker as *const W)) };\n        <W as LocalWake>::wake_by_ref(&waker);\n    }\n\n    // Decrement the reference count of the Rc on drop\n    unsafe fn drop_waker<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n        unsafe { Rc::decrement_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\n    }\n\n    RawWaker::new(\n        Rc::into_raw(waker) as *const (),\n        &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\n    )\n}\n","numLines":351,"startLine":1,"totalLines":351}}}
